     <p><b>McMaster University</b> (commonly referred to as <b>McMaster</b> or <b>Mac</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> whose main campus is located in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The main campus is located on 121 hectares (300&nbsp;acres) of land in the residential neighbourhood of <a href="/wiki/Westdale,_Ontario" title="Westdale, Ontario">Westdale</a>, adjacent to Hamilton's <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Gardens,_Ontario" title="Royal Botanical Gardens, Ontario" class="mw-redirect">Royal Botanical Gardens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MACFF_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACFF-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The university operates six academic faculties: the <a href="/wiki/DeGroote_School_of_Business" title="DeGroote School of Business">DeGroote School of Business</a>, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Engineering" title="McMaster Faculty of Engineering">Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Health_Sciences" title="McMaster Faculty of Health Sciences">Health Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Humanities" title="McMaster Faculty of Humanities">Humanities</a>, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Social_Sciences" title="McMaster Faculty of Social Sciences">Social Science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Science" title="McMaster Faculty of Science">Science</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, a group of research-intensive universities in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university bears the name of Honourable <a href="/wiki/William_McMaster" title="William McMaster">William McMaster</a>, a prominent Canadian <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Canada" title="Senate of Canada">Senator</a> and banker who bequeathed <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">C$</a>900,000 to the founding of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham19853_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham19853-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster University was incorporated under the terms of an act of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Ontario" title="Legislative Assembly of Ontario">Legislative Assembly of Ontario</a> in 1887, merging the Toronto Baptist College with Woodstock College. It opened in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> in 1890. Inadequate facilities and the gift of land in Hamilton prompted the institution to relocate in 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC20_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC20-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster was controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Baptist_Convention_of_Ontario_and_Quebec" title="Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec" class="mw-redirect">Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec</a> until it became a privately chartered, publicly funded non-denominational institution in 1957.</p> 
     <p>The university is co-educational, and has over 24,500 undergraduate and nearly 4,000 post-graduate students. Alumni and former students of the university can be found all across Canada and in 140 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable alumni include government officials, academics, business leaders and two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The university ranked 88th in the 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> 92nd in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and 152nd in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The McMaster athletic teams are known as the <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Marauders" title="McMaster Marauders">Marauders</a>, and are members of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>McMaster University resulted from the outgrowth of educational initiatives undertaken by Baptists as early as the 1830s.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> It was founded in 1881 as Toronto Baptist College. Canadian Senator William McMaster, the first president of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Bank_of_Commerce" title="Canadian Bank of Commerce">Canadian Bank of Commerce</a>, bequeathed funds to endow a university, which was incorporated through a merger of Toronto Baptist College and Woodstock College, <a href="/wiki/Woodstock,_Ontario" title="Woodstock, Ontario">Woodstock, Ontario</a>. In 1887 the Act to unite Toronto Baptist College and Woodstock College was granted <a href="/wiki/Royal_assent" title="Royal assent" class="mw-redirect">royal assent</a>, and McMaster University was officially incorporated.<sup id="cite_ref-AtuTBCaWC_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtuTBCaWC-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Woodstock College, Woodstock, and Moulton Ladies' College, Toronto, were maintained in close connection.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The new university, housed in McMaster Hall in Toronto, was sponsored by the Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec as a sectarian undergraduate institution for its clergy and adherents. The first courses—initially limited to arts and theology leading to a BA degree—were taught in 1890, and the first degrees were conferred in 1894.<sup id="cite_ref-CE_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CE-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RCMPostcard.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Portrait of McMaster Hall, located in Toronto, Ontario" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/RCMPostcard.JPG/220px-RCMPostcard.JPG" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/RCMPostcard.JPG/330px-RCMPostcard.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/RCMPostcard.JPG/440px-RCMPostcard.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RCMPostcard.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> McMaster Hall, located in Toronto, was the original location of the university. The building is currently used as the headquarters for the 
        <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Conservatory_of_Music" title="The Royal Conservatory of Music">The Royal Conservatory of Music</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As the university grew, McMaster Hall started to become overcrowded. The suggestion to move the university to Hamilton was first brought up by a student and Hamilton native in 1909, although the proposal was not seriously considered by the university until two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> By the 1920s, after previous proposals between various university staff, the Hamilton Chamber of Commerce launched a campaign to bring McMaster University to Hamilton.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC20_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC20-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> As the issue of space at McMaster Hall became more acute, the university administration debated the future of the university. The university nearly became federated with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a>, as had been the case with <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College_(U_of_T)" title="Trinity College (U of T)" class="mw-redirect">Trinity College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_College_(U_of_T)" title="Victoria College (U of T)" class="mw-redirect">Victoria College</a>. Instead, in 1927, the university administration decided to transfer the university to Hamilton.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC20_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC20-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec secured $1.5 million, while the citizens of Hamilton raised an additional $500,000 to help finance the move.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC30_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC30-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The lands for the university and new buildings were secured through gifts from graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-CE_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CE-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Lands were transferred from <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Gardens_(Ontario)" title="Royal Botanical Gardens (Ontario)">Royal Botanical Gardens</a> to establish the campus area. The first academic session on the new Hamilton campus began in 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC30_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC30-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster's property in Toronto was sold to the University of Toronto when McMaster moved to Hamilton in 1930. McMaster Hall is now home to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Conservatory_of_Music_(Toronto)" title="Royal Conservatory of Music (Toronto)" class="mw-redirect">Royal Conservatory of Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Professional programs during the interwar period were limited to theology and nursing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGidney200494_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGidney200494-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> By the 1940s the McMaster administration was under pressure to modernize and expand the university's programs. During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War" class="mw-redirect">Second World War</a> and post-war periods the demand for technological expertise, particularly in the sciences, increased.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGidney200494_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGidney200494-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> This problem placed a strain on the finances of what was still a denominational Baptist institution. In particular, the institution could no longer secure sufficient funds from denominational sources alone to sustain science research.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGidney200494_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGidney200494-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Since denominational institutions could not receive public funds, the Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec decided to reorganize the university, creating two federated colleges. The arts and divinity programs were reconstituted as University College and science was reorganized under the newly incorporated Hamilton College as a separate division capable of receiving provincial grants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGidney200494_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGidney200494-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Hamilton College was incorporated in 1948 by letters patent under <i>The Companies Act</i>, although it remained only affiliated with the university.<sup id="cite_ref-BILLPr7_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BILLPr7-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The University traditionally focused on undergraduate studies, and did not offer a PhD program until 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJenkins20046_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJenkins20046-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hamilton Hall at McMaster University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg/200px-Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg/300px-Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg/400px-Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_Hall_at_McMaster_University.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hamilton Hall was constructed in 1926 in preparation for the university's move to Hamilton and now houses the Department of Mathematics &amp; Statistics
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Through the 1950s increased funding advanced the place of sciences within the institution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGidney200495_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGidney200495-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1950, the university had completed the construction of three academic buildings for the sciences, all designed by local architect William Russell Souter.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Public funding was eventually necessary to ensure the humanities and social sciences were given an equal place.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGidney200495_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGidney200495-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Thus, in 1957 the University reorganized once again under <i>The McMaster University Act, 1957</i>, dissolving the two colleges. Its property was vested to McMaster and the university became a nondenominational institution eligible for public funding.<sup id="cite_ref-BILLPr7_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BILLPr7-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The historic Baptist connection was continued through <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Divinity_College" title="McMaster Divinity College">McMaster Divinity College</a>, a separately chartered affiliated college of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-CE_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CE-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MacDiv_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacDiv-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 1957, PhD programs were consolidated in a new Faculty of Graduate Studies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJenkins20046_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJenkins20046-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Construction of the <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Nuclear_Reactor" title="McMaster Nuclear Reactor">McMaster Nuclear Reactor</a> also began in 1957, and was the first university-based <a href="/wiki/Research_reactor" title="Research reactor">research reactor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> when it began operating in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1965, with the support of the Ontario government, the University established a medical school and teaching hospital, graduating its first class of physicians in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1968 the university was reorganized under an amended act of the McMaster Act into the Divisions of Arts, Science, and Health Sciences, each with its own Vice-President, while the Divinity College continued under its existing arrangement.<sup id="cite_ref-BILLPr7_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BILLPr7-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hist2_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hist2-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1974 the divisional structure of the university was dissolved and reorganized again under <i>The McMaster University Act, 1976</i> and the vice-presidents were replaced by a single Vice-President (Academic).<sup id="cite_ref-BILLPr7_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BILLPr7-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The Faculties of Business, Engineering, Health Sciences, Humanities, Science, and Social Sciences were retained, each under the leadership of a dean.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>McMaster University is situated in the city of Hamilton, Ontario, located in the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe" title="Golden Horseshoe">Golden Horseshoe</a> along the western end of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a>. The main campus is bordered to the north by <a href="/wiki/Cootes_Paradise" title="Cootes Paradise">Cootes Paradise</a>, an extensive natural <a href="/wiki/Marshland" title="Marshland" class="mw-redirect">marshland</a>, to the east and west by residential neighbourhoods, and to its south by <a href="/wiki/Main_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="Main Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">Main Street West</a>, a major transportation artery. Its northern boundaries are a popular destination for walkers who make use of the many trails that connect the campus to <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Gardens_(Ontario)" title="Royal Botanical Gardens (Ontario)">Royal Botanical Gardens</a>. While the main campus is 152.4 hectares (377&nbsp;acres), the majority of the teaching facilities are centered within the core 12.1 hectares (30&nbsp;acres).<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MACFF_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACFF-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to its main campus in Hamilton, McMaster owns several other properties around Hamilton, as well as in <a href="/wiki/Burlington,_Ontario" title="Burlington, Ontario">Burlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kitchener,_Ontario" title="Kitchener, Ontario">Kitchener</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Catharines" title="St. Catharines">St. Catharines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>.</p> 
     <p>The university owns and manages 62 buildings, both on and off campus.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The buildings at McMaster vary in age, with Hamilton Hall opening in 1926, to the university's new nuclear research facility, which opened in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC20_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC20-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Plans to construct a new academic building in 2013, known as the Wilson Building for Studies in Humanities and Social Sciences, are underway after securing a substantial donation from the university's chancellor, <a href="/wiki/Lynton_Wilson" title="Lynton Wilson">Lynton Wilson</a>, as well as securing funding from the provincial government.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster main campus is divided up into three main areas: the Core Campus, North Campus and West Campus. The Core Campus is where the majority of the university's academic, research and residential buildings are located while the North Campus is made up of the university's athletic precinct and a small amount of surface parking. The West Campus is the least developed area of the main campus, containing only a few buildings, surface parking, and undeveloped land.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:708px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG" class="image" title="Panoramic view of McMaster University from the southwest, taken on June 2008"><img alt="Panoramic Image of McMaster University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG/700px-Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG" width="700" height="137" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG/1050px-Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG/1400px-Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG 2x" /></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pan-IMGP0137-IMGP0142-mod-and-crop.JPG" title="Enlarge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" /></a>
        </div> Panoramic view of McMaster University from the southwest, taken on June 2008
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_facilities">Academic facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Academic facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="University Hall at McMaster University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg/200px-McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg/300px-McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg/400px-McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McMaster_University_-_University_Hall_tower_and_archway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University Hall displays a Gothic Revival architectural style
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Conhall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Conhall.jpg/200px-Conhall.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Conhall.jpg/300px-Conhall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Conhall.jpg/400px-Conhall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Conhall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Close up of University Hall and its Gothic Architecture
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university's campus has gone through continuous development since 1928. The main campus's six original buildings are of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">neo-Gothic</a> architecture. They are now flanked by over fifty structures built predominantly during booms in the 1950s, 1960s and during the 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest facility is the McMaster University Medical Centre, a multi-use research hospital that is home to the second-largest neonatal intensive care unit and the third-largest child and youth mental health unit in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> It is connected to the Life Sciences building and the Michael DeGroote Centre for Learning &amp; Discovery, which houses many well-funded research groups in areas of <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Infectious_diseases" title="Infectious diseases" class="mw-redirect">infectious diseases</a>, and several specific conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The McMaster Nuclear Reactor (MNR) has been the largest university reactor in the Commonwealth since it began operation and is the second largest research reactor in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-MacNU_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacNU-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> It is a &quot;pool-type&quot; reactor with a core of <a href="/wiki/Enriched_uranium" title="Enriched uranium">enriched uranium</a> fuel moderated and cooled by <a href="/wiki/Distilled_water" title="Distilled water">distilled water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> While the MNR's primary purpose is research and the production of <a href="/wiki/Medical_isotopes" title="Medical isotopes" class="mw-redirect">medical isotopes</a>, the MNR also serves students in nuclear engineering, medical and health physics, and other applied radiation sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university provides a wide range of irradiation, laboratory, and holding facilities, which include a <a href="/wiki/Cyclotron" title="Cyclotron">cyclotron</a>, an accelerator, a small-angle neutron-scattering detector, and wide-angle neutron scattering facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-mnr_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnr-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The cyclotron is used for the production of <a href="/wiki/Fluorine-18" title="Fluorine-18">fluorine-18</a>, and is used for research purposes, particularly the development of novel molecular imaging agents.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library_and_museum">Library and museum</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Library and museum">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university's library system is a member of 31 organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Research_Libraries" title="Association of Research Libraries">Association of Research Libraries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The library's resource expenditure on 30 April 2010 was approximately $7.8 million, with 83.8 percent of the budget allocated to serial subscriptions, and 15.3 percent on hard copy acquisitions.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The library system include four libraries housing 1,645,876 volumes and 3,620,092 total resources, including videos, maps, sound recordings, and microfilm.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Mills Library houses the humanities and social sciences collections, with a wide range of print and digital resources. Innis Library houses content which supports the academic and research interests of the DeGroote School of Business. Thode Library houses academic material of various disciplines of science and engineering, while the Health Science Library houses books pertaining to medical sciences. The William Ready Division of Archives and Research Collections at McMaster University consist of papers of Canadian publishers; British personalities and of Canadian literary figures such as <a href="/wiki/Farley_Mowat" title="Farley Mowat">Farley Mowat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Berton" title="Pierre Berton">Pierre Berton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Cohen_(writer)" title="Matt Cohen (writer)">Matt Cohen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marian_Engel" title="Marian Engel">Marian Engel</a>. It includes the archives of <a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Russell" title="Bertrand Russell">Bertrand Russell</a>, and of labour unions.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Museum_of_Art" title="McMaster Museum of Art">McMaster Museum of Art</a>'s (MMA) principal role is to support the academic mission of McMaster University and to contribute to the discourse on art in Canada. The museum has the highest attendance figures for a university-affiliated museum in Canada, with 30,040 visitors. Established in 1967, the museum houses and exhibits the university's art collection.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2010, that collection of 6,980 pieces holds a total value of $98 million.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The collection includes works by <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Courbet" title="Gustave Courbet">Gustave Courbet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Monet" title="Claude Monet">Claude Monet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camille_Pissarro" title="Camille Pissarro">Camille Pissarro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Sickert" title="Walter Sickert">Walter Sickert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Vincent van Gogh</a>. The museum also boasts the most comprehensive collection of <a href="/wiki/German_Expressionism" title="German Expressionism">German expressionist</a> and Weimar period prints in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_and_student_facilities">Housing and student facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Housing and student facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Edward's Hall with Chester New Hall in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg/200px-Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg/300px-Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg/400px-Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Edwards_Hall_McMaster_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Edward's Hall is one of twelve student residences located within the main campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Currently McMaster has twelve smoke-free student residences: Bates, Brandon, Edwards, Hedden, Les Prince, Mary E. Keyes, Matthews, McKay, Moulton, Wallingford, Whidden, and Woodstock Hall. McMaster's student residences can accommodate 3,685 students in total.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The latest residence to be built was Les Prince Hall, a large co-ed building, completed in 2006. It was named for a long-time hall master in the residence system who lived with his family on campus until after his retirement in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2010, 49 percent of first-year students lived on campus, with 17.1 percent of the overall undergraduate population living on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Residences provide traditional room and board style, furnished apartment style, and suite-style accommodation. Brandon Hall houses the university's substance-free lifestyle living spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The residence system is supervised by Residence Life staff, who provide guidance and help the transition to university life for many first-year students.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Residence students are represented by the Inter-Residence Council (IRC), which aims to build a sense of community among the residents through programming.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The McMaster University Student Centre (MUSC) is the centre of student life and programming. It contains a caf&eacute;, study space, common areas, and a number of administrative departments, including the CIBC Conference Hall. The MUSC contains the offices of a number of student organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Students_Union" title="McMaster Students Union">McMaster Students Union</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silhouette" title="The Silhouette">The Silhouette</a></i> weekly newspaper as well as other services such as the Campus Health Centre and the campus dentist.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has over twenty dining outlets located throughout the campus, including two major residence dining facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has a number of vegetarian establishments, such as a completely vegetarian cafe known as Bridges Caf&eacute; and a farmers market stand. The university was voted as the country's most vegan-friendly university through <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals</a> (PETA) for a number of years.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Several other dining outlets at McMaster have garnered a number of awards throughout the years for food services.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Off-campus_facilities">Off-campus facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Off-campus facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of 2010 McMaster University's DeGroote School of Business operates a 1.82-hectare (4.5-acre) site in the neighbouring city of Burlington. Consideration for the new building began in 2004, when McMaster University had announced its initial intent to construct a new arts- and technology-intensive campus in partnership with the city of Burlington. In 2009, the City of Burlington, Halton Region, and McMaster University signed an official agreement laying out the timelines and next steps for the university's expansion into Burlington.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Construction began on 17 June 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> and the official opening was on 7 October 2010. The four-story, 90,000-square-foot (8,400&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) building is called the Ron Joyce Centre. The Ron Joyce Centre is home to DeGroote's MBA program and its business management program (both degree and non-degree programs).<sup id="cite_ref-MCRJC_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCRJC-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McMaster has a number of administrative offices at its Downtown Centre, located in Hamilton in the former Wentworth County Courthouse.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The centre is also home to the McMaster Centre for Continuing Education, which offers a variety of certificate and diploma programs as well as personal and professional development programs.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Michael G. DeGroote School of Medicine is located on the main campus as well as in two regional campses at St. Catharines and Kitchener. The Waterloo Regional Campus is located in downtown Kitchener, sharing facilities with the Health Sciences Campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo" title="University of Waterloo">University of Waterloo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus in St. Catharines is located at <a href="/wiki/Brock_University" title="Brock University">Brock University's</a> Niagara Health and Bioscience Research Complex.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 30 medical students in each year of the program attend each campus.<sup id="cite_ref-MedScho_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MedScho-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Those who apply to McMaster's School of Medicine are asked to rank their site choice (Hamilton, Niagara Region, Waterloo Region) from first to third, or no preference. Offers of admission to the medical school are made from a rank list irrespective of geographical preference. Subsequent to an applicant's acceptance, registrants to the class are placed based on their preference and geographical background. The offers given out by McMaster are bound to the assigned site.<sup id="cite_ref-MedScho_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MedScho-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McMaster purchased a large industrial park three kilometres east of its main Hamilton campus in 2005 with the intention of creating an array of research facilities for the development of advanced manufacturing and materials, biotechnology, automotive, and nanotechnology.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> In July 2005 the federal government announced that it would be relocating CANMET, a federal government materials research laboratory, from its <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a> centre to Hamilton. This decision helped spearhead the development of the <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Innovation_Park" title="McMaster Innovation Park">McMaster Innovation Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_University" title="United Nations University">United Nations University</a>-International Network on Water, Environment and Health (UNU-INWEH) is currently headquartered within the park. UNU-INWEH is the only United Nations agency headquartered in Ontario and the only North American host site for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_University" title="United Nations University">United Nations University</a>, after moving to McMaster Innovation Park on 23 April 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-MACFF_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACFF-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Office of Sustainability, created as the All-modes Commuting &amp; Transportation Office in 2002, is charged with promoting sustainable operations and growth at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The Office of Sustainability, headed by the Manager of University Sustainability, works with members of the university population, external community groups, and the government.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Along with the other members of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ontario_Universities" title="Council of Ontario Universities">Council of Ontario Universities</a>, McMaster signed a pledge in 2009 known as <i>Ontario Universities Committed to a Greener World</i>, with the objective of transforming its campus into a model of environmental responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> On 21 October 2010, the university signed two accords addressing the issue of climate change: the <a href="/wiki/Talloires_Declaration" title="Talloires Declaration">Talloires Declaration</a> and the <i>University and College Presidents’ Climate Change Statement of Action for Canada</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university campus received a B grade from the Sustainable Endowments Institute on its College Sustainability Report Card for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;" align="right"> 
      <caption>
       <b>Current Faculties of McMaster University</b>
      </caption> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <th><b>Faculties</b><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <th><b>Established</b></th> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td><a href="/wiki/DeGroote_School_of_Business" title="DeGroote School of Business">DeGroote School of Business</a></td> 
        <td>1952<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td><a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Engineering" title="McMaster Faculty of Engineering">Faculty of Engineering</a></td> 
        <td>1958<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td><a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Health_Sciences" title="McMaster Faculty of Health Sciences">Faculty of Health Sciences</a></td> 
        <td>1974<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td><a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Humanities" title="McMaster Faculty of Humanities">Faculty of Humanities</a></td> 
        <td>1887</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td><a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Science" title="McMaster Faculty of Science">Faculty of Science</a></td> 
        <td>1887</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td><a href="/wiki/McMaster_Faculty_of_Social_Sciences" title="McMaster Faculty of Social Sciences">Faculty of Social Sciences</a></td> 
        <td>1887</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The governance of the university is conducted through the Board of Governors and the Senate, both of which were established in the Act to unite Toronto Baptist College and Woodstock College in 1887.<sup id="cite_ref-AtuTBCaWC_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtuTBCaWC-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board is responsible for the university's conduct, management, and control of the university and of its property, revenues, business, and affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-MUA76_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUA76-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Ex officio governors of the Board include the university's chancellor, president, and the chairman of the board-senate committee on long-range planning. The Board also consists of 34 other governors, either appointed or elected by the various members of the university's community, including elected representatives from the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-MUA76_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUA76-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> While The McMaster University Act, 1976 outlines that the board be only composed of 37 members, the Board also includes 12 honorary members, bringing the total number of governors to 51.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Senate is responsible for the university's academics, including standards for admission into the university and qualifications for degrees, diplomas, and certificates.<sup id="cite_ref-MUA76_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUA76-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate consists of 15 ex officio positions granted to the chancellor, the president, the vice-presidents of the university, the senior dean of each faculty, the dean of graduate studies, the dean of adult education, the principal of McMaster Divinity College, and the Chairman of the Undergraduate Council. The Senate also consists of 51 other members, appointed or elected by the various communities of the university including elected representatives of the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Meetings of the Board of Governors and the Senate are open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-MUA76_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUA76-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The president acts as the chief executive officer of the university under the authority of the Board and the Senate, and supervises and directs the academic and administrative work of the university and of its teaching and non-teaching staff.<sup id="cite_ref-MUA76_76-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUA76-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Deane_(professor)" title="Patrick Deane (professor)">Patrick Deane</a> is the seventh president of the university, serving the post since 1 July 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The office was created in 1949, with <a href="/wiki/George_Gilmour" title="George Gilmour">George Gilmour</a> serving as the university's first president. The office of the vice-chancellor, created at the same time as the office of president, has always been held by the incumbent president of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Programs, departments, and schools at McMaster are divided among six faculties. By enrolment, the three largest programs are engineering, with 3,662 full-time and part-time students, followed by the social sciences, with 5,014 full-time and part-time undergraduates and graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The School of Graduate Studies serves as the central administrative unit of graduate education at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The School of Graduate Studies is not considered its own faculty. The <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Arts_and_Science" title="McMaster Arts and Science">Arts and Science program</a> is taught jointly by the other faculties at McMaster.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJenkins200432_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJenkins200432-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Created in 1981, the program aims to provide a broad-based, liberal education, providing substantial work in both the arts and sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJenkins20043_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJenkins20043-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The total net assets owned by the university as of 30 April 2012 stands at $705.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-MacFin_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacFin-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The university had completed the 2011–2012 year with revenues of $877.9 million, expenses of $868.7 million and an excess of revenues over expenses of $9.1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-MacFin_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacFin-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster's revenue comes from endowment income, gifts, fees, and annual grants from the City of Hamilton, the Hamilton-Wentworth Region, the Province of Ontario, and the Government of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Hist2_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hist2-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The majority of McMaster's financial revenue originates from financial endowments. The second-largest source of revenue is operating grants provided by the government, valued at nearly C$232.9 million. As of 30 April 2012, McMaster's financial endowment was valued at C$519.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-MacFin_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacFin-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The financing of McMaster's scholarships and bursaries takes up 40 per cent of the endowments received.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Financial Services comprises the following areas: Student Accounts &amp; Cashiers, Financial Accounting and Reporting, and Budgeting Services.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has been registered as an educational charitable organization in Canada since 1 January 1967. As of 2011, the university has registered the university primarily as a post-secondary institution, with 70 percent of the charity dedicated to the management and maintenance of the university. The remaining 30 percent has been dedicated under research.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>McMaster is a publicly funded research university, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster functions on a semester system, operating year-round on academic semesters, fall/winter and spring/summer.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Undergraduate programs comprise the majority of the school's enrolment, made up of 24,520 full-time and part-time undergraduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The university conferred 4,690 bachelor degrees, 221 doctoral degrees, 993 master degrees, and 179 first professional degrees in 2010–2011.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students may apply for financial aid such as the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Student_Assistance_Program" title="Ontario Student Assistance Program">Ontario Student Assistance Program</a> and <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_Canada" title="Student loans in Canada">Canada Student Loans and Grants</a> through the federal and provincial governments. The financial aid provided may come in the form of loans, grants, bursaries, scholarships, fellowships, debt reduction, interest relief, and work programs.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010–11, McMaster students received $70.3 million in Canada-Ontario Integrated Student Loans and $17.3 million in grants, approximately $87.7 million in total.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="McMaster_Model">McMaster Model</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: McMaster Model">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The McMaster Model is the university's policy for a student-centred, problem-based, interdisciplinary approach to learning, a policy which has been adopted by several other universities around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-MACFF_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACFF-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 1960s the university's Faculty of Health Science pioneered <a href="/wiki/Problem-based_learning" title="Problem-based learning">problem-based learning</a> (PBL) tutorials that have since been adopted by other programs and faculties within the university. PBL is now used in occupational therapy, physical therapy, nursing, midwifery, and other allied fields.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Most medical schools in Canada and more than 80 percent of medical schools in the United States employ PBL in their curriculum, and many international universities do the same.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1991, McMaster's <a href="/wiki/Michael_G._DeGroote_School_of_Medicine" title="Michael G. DeGroote School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a> adopted <a href="/wiki/Progress_testing" title="Progress testing">progress testing</a>, developing the personal progress index (PPI), a system based on progress testing invented concurrently by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri-Kansas_City" title="University of Missouri-Kansas City" class="mw-redirect">University of Missouri-Kansas City</a>'s medical school and the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_University" title="Maastricht University">Maastricht University</a>. The PPI is used as an objective method for assessing acquisition and retention of knowledge for students in the medical program.<sup id="cite_ref-ACAMED_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACAMED-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The PPI is administered at regular intervals to all students in the program, regardless of their level of training, and plots students' scores as they move through the program. Students typically score 20 percent on their first examination, and increase by five to seven percent with each successive examination.<sup id="cite_ref-ACAMED_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACAMED-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Students can monitor the changes in their scores and receive formative feedback based on a standardized score relative to the class mean.<sup id="cite_ref-ACAMED_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACAMED-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to the overwhelming success and research supporting the use of the PPI as an evaluation tool, it is now used in Canada, US, Europe, and Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a>]</span></h3>

           <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template:Canadian university rankings"><span title="View this template" style="">v</span></a></li>

           <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Canadian_university_rankings&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template" style="">e</span></a></li>
