     <p>McMaster University has consistently been ranked one of Canada's top universities. In the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU) rankings, the university ranked 92nd in the world and fourth-highest in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012–2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> placed McMaster 88th in the world, and fifth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> ranked the university 152nd in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a> had also ranked McMaster as the 15th top university outside of the United States, and the fourth best university in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of national rankings, <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> ranked McMaster 6th in their 2012 Medical Doctoral university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster was ranked in spite of having opted out—along with several other universities in Canada—of participating in Maclean's graduate survey since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McMaster's Health Science program has consistently been ranked within the top 100 universities. In the 2012–2013 Times Higher Education rankings of clinical, pre-clinical, and health universities, McMaster's Health Science program ranked 14th in the world and first in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_HEAL_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_HEAL-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2013 QS World University Rankings had ranked the medical program at McMaster 42nd in the world, and fourth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> In the ARWU 2012 rankings for the field of clinical medicine and pharmacy, the university had placed 46th in the world and third in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_MED_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_MED-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster was also ranked in a number of ARWU rankings based on academic fields. The university was ranked 42nd in the ARWU 2012 in the field of social sciences, the second-highest in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same 2012 ARWU rankings, the university had ranked 101–150th in the field of natural science and mathematics, and ranked 151–200th in the field of engineering and computer science.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SCI_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SCI-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_ENG_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_ENG-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster's DeGroote School of Business has garnered national and worldwide recognition, as it was accredited by the <a href="/wiki/AACSB" title="AACSB" class="mw-redirect">AACSB</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> In an employability survey published by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a> in October 2011, when CEOs and chairmans were asked to select the top universities which they recruited from, McMaster placed 61st in the world, and fourth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In Research Infosource's <i>Decade in Review</i>, McMaster was designated the top performer in research income growth from 1999 to 2009 in the medical doctoral category and as the second-top performer in research intensity growth for the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-RIMAC_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIMAC-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> With a total sponsored research income of $377.732 million, McMaster has the sixth largest sponsored research income in the country. With an average research income of $310,100 CAD per full-time faculty member, McMaster is also the second most research intensive full-service university in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004 McMaster earned the designation of research university of the year based on its ability to attract and capitalize on its research income.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Its research activities exceed those of universities twice its size. The federal government is the largest source of funding, providing 57 percent of McMaster's research budget, primarily through grants. Corporations contribute around 12 percent of the overall research budget.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg/220px-Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg" width="220" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg/330px-Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg/440px-Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nuclear_Reactor_McMaster_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Nuclear_Reactor" title="McMaster Nuclear Reactor">McMaster Nuclear Reactor</a> is the largest research reactor in the 
        <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In terms of research performance, <a href="/wiki/High_Impact_Universities" title="High Impact Universities">High Impact Universities</a> 2010 ranked McMaster 62nd out of 500 universities, and fourth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was ranked 25th out of 500 universities—second in the country—for research performance in the fields of medicine, dentistry, pharmacology, and health sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was ranked 83rd out of 500 universities, ranking third nationally, for research performance in the fields of engineering, computing, and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In the fields of arts, humanities, business, and social sciences, the university's research performance was ranked 60th out of 500 universities, the third highest nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Canada#Higher_Education_Strategy_Associates.27_rankings" title="Rankings of universities in Canada">Higher Education Strategy Associates</a>, another organization which also ranks universities on the basis of their research strength, ranked McMaster tenth nationally in the field of science and engineering and seventh nationally in the field of social sciences and humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT), an organization which also evaluates universities based on their <a href="/wiki/Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" title="Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities">scientific paper's performances</a>, ranked McMaster 54th in the world and fourth nationally for in social sciences in its 2011 rankings. HEEACT placed McMaster 95th in the world and fifth nationally for its overall research performance.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McMaster has been has received accolades for its research strengths, particularly in the field of health sciences. For five years in a row, McMaster has ranked second in for biomedical and health care research revenues by the Association of Faculties of Medicine of Canada. In 2008–2009, Faculty investigators were overseeing $133 million a year in research, much of that research conducted by scientists and physicians who teach in the medical school.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> For its 2011 rankings, HEEACT ranked McMaster 35th in the world and third on a national scale for scientific papers in <a href="/wiki/Clinical_medicine" title="Clinical medicine" class="mw-redirect">clinical medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The Faculty of Health Sciences operates several research institutes, including the Farncombe Family Digestive Health Research Institute, the DeGroote Institute for Infectious Disease Research, and the Stem Cell and Cancer Research Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> A McMaster research group led by <a href="/wiki/David_Sackett" title="David Sackett">David Sackett</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Guyatt" title="Gordon Guyatt">Gordon Guyatt</a> had been largely credited for largely establishing the methodologies used in <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_medicine" title="Evidence-based medicine">evidence-based medicine</a>. Guyatt had also been credited for coining the term evidence-based medicine in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2010, researchers at the Stem Cell and Cancer Research Institute turned clumps of human skin into blood cells, which may help alleviate the shortage of <a href="/wiki/Blood_donation" title="Blood donation">blood donors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> A portion of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein%27s_brain" title="Albert Einstein's brain">Albert Einstein's brain</a> is preserved and held for medical research at the McMaster brain bank.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Researchers there have identified differences in his brain that may relate to his genius for spatial and mathematical thinking.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Brockhouse Institute for Material Research (BIMR) is located at McMaster. Created in 1960 by <a href="/wiki/Howard_Petch" title="Howard Petch">Howard Petch</a>, the institute was named after McMaster alumnus <a href="/wiki/Bertram_Brockhouse" title="Bertram Brockhouse">Bertram Brockhouse</a>. The BIMR is an interdisciplinary research organization with the mandate to develop, support, and co-ordinate all materials research related activities at McMaster.<sup id="cite_ref-BIMR_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIMR-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Its membership of 123 faculty members is drawn from 13 departments in the Faculties of Science, Engineering, and Health Sciences, as well as several Canadian and international universities.<sup id="cite_ref-BIMR_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIMR-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Facilities of the BIMR include the Canadian Centre for Electron Microscopy, Centre for Crystal Growth, McMaster Analytical Xray Facility, Electronic and Magnetic Characterization Facility, and the Photonics Research Laboratories.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The Canadian Centre for Electron Microscopy is home to the world's most advanced microscope. The Titan 80–300 cubed microscope has a magnification of 14 million and is used for material, medical, and <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a> research.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also operates the McMaster Nuclear Reactor, which has been used for nuclear science and engineering research since 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-mnr_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnr-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The strength of nuclear science at McMaster was augmented in 1968 under the presidency of Dr. <a href="/wiki/Harry_Thode" title="Harry Thode">H.G. Thode</a> by the construction of a 10MV Model FN Tandem <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">particle accelerator</a>. The 3MV Model KN single-ended accelerator was added the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The academic direction of the laboratory fell to the Physics Department in the early days, as it was primarily a nuclear structure laboratory. During the next 28 years, the nuclear research effort was extensive, with hundreds of graduate students trained and many publications generated.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> The reactor at McMaster produces 25 percent of the world's supply of <a href="/wiki/Iodine-125" title="Iodine-125">iodine-125</a>, an isotope used in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_medicine" title="Nuclear medicine">nuclear medicine</a> to treat prostate cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-MacNU_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacNU-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The production of <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum-99" title="Molybdenum-99" class="mw-redirect">molybdenum-99</a> at the <a href="/wiki/National_Research_Universal_Reactor" title="National Research Universal Reactor" class="mw-redirect">National Research Universal Reactor</a> (NRU) has also been occasionally moved to the university's reactor, during the 1970 and <a href="/wiki/Chalk_River_Laboratories#2009_NRU_Reactor_shutdown" title="Chalk River Laboratories">2009 shutdown</a> of the NRU.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster University's SLOWPOKE-2 non-power reactor operating licence is valid until June 30, 2014. The <a href="/wiki/SLOWPOKE_reactor" title="SLOWPOKE reactor">SLOWPOKE reactor</a> is used for research and education, commercial applications such as neutron radiography, and medical radioisotope production; Iodine-125 is used in cancer therapy.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The requirements for admission differ between students from Ontario, other provinces in Canada, and international students due to the lack of uniformity in marking schemes. The acceptance rate at McMaster for full-time, first-year applications in 2012 was 59 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2011, the secondary school average for full-time first-year students at McMaster University was 86.3 percent. Students entering McMaster's more selective undergraduate programs, such as its Health Science program and its Arts and Science program, had a secondary school average of 95.8 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McMaster's medical school receives twice the number of applications as other medical programs in Canada, with more than 4,500 applicants competing for 204 positions.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2001 McMaster developed the <a href="/wiki/Multiple_Mini_Interview" title="Multiple Mini Interview" class="mw-redirect">multiple-mini interview</a> to address long-standing concerns over the standard panel interviews as being poor reflectors of performance in medical school.<sup id="cite_ref-macmmi_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macmmi-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> This format uses short, independent assessments in a timed circuit to obtain aggregate scores in interpersonal skills, professionalism, ethical/moral judgment, and critical thinking to assess candidates. The multiple-mini interview has consistently shown to have a higher predictive validity for future performance than traditional interviews.<sup id="cite_ref-macmmi_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macmmi-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> The format has since been adopted by the majority of other medical schools in Canada and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_groups">Student groups</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Student groups">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="McMaster University Student Centre and Mills Memorial Library" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg/220px-McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg/330px-McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg/440px-McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McMasterUnionStudentCentre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The McMaster University Student Centre houses a number of student groups, including the 
        <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Students_Union" title="McMaster Students Union">McMaster Students Union</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The main student unions on administrative and policy issues are the <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Students_Union" title="McMaster Students Union">McMaster Students Union</a> for full-time undergraduates, the McMaster Association of Part-Time Students for part-time undergraduates, and the McMaster Graduate Students Association for postgraduates.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, each faculty has its own student representative body. Students within the residence are represented by the Inter-Residence Council.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> There are more than 200 student organizations and clubs, covering a wide range of interests such as academics, culture, religion, social issues, and recreation.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of them are centred on the McMaster <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student activity centre</a>, the McMaster University Student Centre. <i>The Silhouette</i>, the student-run newspaper, is the oldest student service at McMaster University, in publication since 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-MAC20_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAC20-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1968, the McMaster Engineering Society has published <i>The Plumbline</i>, the main satire magazine of McMaster University.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">campus radio</a> station <a href="/wiki/CFMU-FM" title="CFMU-FM">CFMU-FM</a> (93.3 <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio" class="mw-redirect">FM</a>) is Canada’s second-oldest campus radio station, and has been broadcasting since 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> MacInsiders, a popular online student-run forum and information network, has been operating since 2007<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> and has over 18,000 registered members.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The McMaster Marching Band, created in September 2009, is a brass and reed <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a> composed of 35 graduate and undergraduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university hosts a number of honour societies, including the McMaster Honour Society and a chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Key_International_Honour_Society" title="Golden Key International Honour Society">Golden Key International Honour Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is home to two semi-professional acting companies, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Musical_Theatre" title="McMaster Musical Theatre">McMaster Musical Theatre</a> and the McMaster Thespian Company.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> The McMaster Engineering Musical is an annual musical production that is written, directed, and cast by engineers. The production often features unique interpretations of popular songs or musicals.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> The university and the student unions do not recognize any <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternity or sororities</a>; existing chapters operate as non-accredited off-campus organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Six fraternities currently operate an active chapter at the university; <a href="/wiki/Pi_Kappa_Alpha" title="Pi Kappa Alpha">Pi Kappa Alpha</a> , Nu Omega Sigma, Omicron Pi Alpha, Lambda Phi Epsilon, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a> and four Sororities including Tau Sigma Phi, Nu Omega Zeta, Epsilon Sigma Alpha, and Delta Pi.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Marauders" title="McMaster Marauders">McMaster Marauders</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Marauders_football" title="McMaster Marauders football">McMaster Marauders football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Welcome Week Football Game, McMaster University. September 2009." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg/225px-McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg" width="225" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg/338px-McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg/450px-McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McMaster_University_-_Welcome_Week_football_game.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Marauders_football" title="McMaster Marauders football">McMaster Marauders football team</a> at Ron Joyce Stadium
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Athletics at McMaster is managed by the university's student affairs, under their athletics and recreation department. The university's varsity teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference of the Canadian Interuniversity Sport. The university's team sports programs include baseball, basketball, football, lacrosse, rugby, soccer, volleyball, and water polo. The first major sport game played at McMaster was in 1889, when a group of alumni from Toronto Baptist College and Woodstock College played an exhibition game against one another, sparking an early intercity rivalry between McMaster students. In 1897 the university placed all physical activity and sports under the jurisdiction of a central executive committee.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The varsity teams have been known as the McMaster Marauders since 1948, through a contest run by the student newspaper, The Silhouette, to name the university's men's basketball team.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Marauders have won 11 national championships and 139 provincial champions since 1961. The men's water polo team has won the Ontario University Athletics championship 25 times, making it the Marauders' most successful team at the provincial level. The men's wrestling team has been the Marauders' most successful team at the national level, winning the Canadian Interuniversity Sport championship four times.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster University has graduated 34 <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> athletes, eight Olympic coaches, two Olympic administrators and two Olympic officials.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> As is mandatory for all members of Canadian Interuniversity Sport, McMaster University does not provide full-ride athletic scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's sports facilities are located in the northeast corner of the main campus. The university has a number of sports facilities, including the <a href="/wiki/David_Braley_Athletic_Centre" title="David Braley Athletic Centre">David Braley Athletic Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ron_Joyce_Stadium" title="Ron Joyce Stadium">Ron Joyce Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Ron Joyce Stadium includes a full-sized Canadian football field and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>-sized soccer pitch. The stadium features permanent seating for 6,000 and temporary seating for an additional 6,000 on the other side of the field when needed. Ron Joyce Stadium is not only used by the university's football and soccer varsity teams it is also used as the training camp for the <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Tiger-Cats" title="Hamilton Tiger-Cats">Hamilton Tiger-Cats</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a> and as the home stadium for the <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Nationals" title="Hamilton Nationals">Hamilton Nationals</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Lacrosse" title="Major League Lacrosse">Major League Lacrosse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Intramural sport leagues and tournaments have a high level of participation at McMaster. Opportunities are offered at multiple skill levels and across a variety of sports to service a range of interest and ability. Sports offered include traditional sports like volleyball, basketball, soccer and cricket, as well as less traditional events like <a href="/wiki/Dodgeball" title="Dodgeball">dodgeball</a>, inner tube water polo, and extreme potato sack racing.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Insignias_and_other_representations">Insignias and other representations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Insignias and other representations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motto_and_songs">Motto and songs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Motto and songs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The McMaster motto, chosen from <a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Colossians" title="Epistle to the Colossians">Colossians</a> 1:17, is <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">ΤΑ ΠΑΝΤΑ ΕΝ ΧΡΙΣΤΩΙ ΣΥΝΕΣΤΗΚΕΝ</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-RegisterofArms_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RegisterofArms-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> The motto, adopted in 1888, is Greek for &quot;In Christ all things consists&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-RegisterofArms_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RegisterofArms-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> The McMaster motto is unusual in that it employs Greek instead of Latin or English. The use of Latin reflects the origin of universities in mediaeval institutions in which Latin was more prominent than Greek.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham19853_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham19853-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MACMOT_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACMOT-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> McMaster's founders desired to go back beyond the Middle Ages to the earliest days of the Christian faith, and therefore used the Greek form.<sup id="cite_ref-MACMOT_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACMOT-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are: <i>The Alma Mater Song</i> (1935), with words by Mrs. A.A. Burridge and music by Hugh Brearly; <i>The McMaster March</i>, with words by Claire Senior Burke et al., and music by Arthur Burridge; and <i>My Mac</i> (1982), with words and music by Fred Moyes.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>After the university moved to Hamilton in 1930, the university petitioned <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon_King_of_Arms" title="Lord Lyon King of Arms">Lord Lyon King of Arms</a> in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MACCOA_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACCOA-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> The request was granted on behalf of <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">The Crown</a> on 20 October 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham19853_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham19853-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MACCOA_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACCOA-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1997 the Board of Governors introduced a simplified shield design, which recognized the tradition of McMaster’s heraldry while improving the quality of print and electronic reproduction.<sup id="cite_ref-MACCOA_173-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACCOA-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's arms and badge was registered with the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Heraldic_Authority" title="Canadian Heraldic Authority">Canadian Heraldic Authority</a> on 15 October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The coat of arms consists of a shield, a crest, and a motto, together with a <a href="/wiki/Helmet_(heraldry)" title="Helmet (heraldry)">helmet</a>. The shield contains an eagle, symbolic of the heavenly vision, with a cross on its breast to indicate Christianity as the inspiration for the university's vision.<sup id="cite_ref-shield_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shield-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chief_(heraldry)" title="Chief (heraldry)">chief</a> of the shield bears an open book, a common symbol of learning, with a maple leaf on each side, signifying that McMaster's charter was granted by the Province of Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-shield_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shield-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> The helmet, above the shield, has the open visor and forward-facing style typically used by universities.<sup id="cite_ref-shield_175-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shield-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mantling" title="Mantling">mantling</a> surrounding the shield and helmet represents the cloak worn over a knight's armour as protection from the sun. The crest, located above the helmet, is a stag and oak tree, which serves as a tribute to the Canadian Senator, William McMaster, who also used a stag and oak on his insignias.<sup id="cite_ref-MACCOA_173-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MACCOA-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> The motto is located above the crest, as is common in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_heraldry" title="Scottish heraldry">Scottish heraldry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McMaster_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tommycropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Tommy Douglas stands in front of a group of men in military uniform." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Tommycropped.jpg/170px-Tommycropped.jpg" width="170" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Tommycropped.jpg/255px-Tommycropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Tommycropped.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tommycropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Douglas" title="Tommy Douglas">Tommy Douglas</a>, former premier of Saskatchewan and alumnus of McMaster
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_McMaster_University_people" title="List of McMaster University people">List of McMaster University people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_McMaster_University_Olympic_athletes,_coaches_and_officials" title="List of McMaster University Olympic athletes, coaches and officials">List of McMaster University Olympic athletes, coaches and officials</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As of November 2010, McMaster University has over 140,000 alumni residing over 140 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-fbook_3-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Throughout McMaster's history, faculty, alumni, and former students have played prominent roles in many different fields, accumulating a number of awards including <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prizes" title="Nobel Prizes" class="mw-redirect">Nobel prizes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarships" title="Rhodes Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes scholarships</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lasker_Award" title="Lasker Award">Lasker Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Nobel Prize winners include alumnus <a href="/wiki/Myron_Scholes" title="Myron Scholes">Myron Scholes</a>, who was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a> in 1997; faculty member Bertram Brockhouse, who was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> in 1994; and alumnus <a href="/wiki/James_Orbinski" title="James Orbinski">James Orbinski</a>, who accepted the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> in 1992 on behalf of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="M&eacute;decins Sans Fronti&egrave;res">Doctors Without Borders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many former students have gained local and national prominence for serving in government. <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Alexander" title="Lincoln Alexander">Lincoln Alexander</a> served as <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Ontario" title="Lieutenant Governor of Ontario">Lieutenant Governor of Ontario</a>, also becoming the first visible-minority Lieutenant Governor in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Two premiers from Canada, the former <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Ontario" title="Premier of Ontario">premier from Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalton_McGuinty" title="Dalton McGuinty">Dalton McGuinty</a>, and the former <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Saskatchewan" title="Premier of Saskatchewan">premier of Saskatchewan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Douglas" title="Tommy Douglas">Tommy Douglas</a>, were graduates of McMaster University.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> Prominent faculty members in the field of social sciences include <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Landes" title="Ruth Landes">Ruth Landes</a>, a cultural anthropologist, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Giroux" title="Henry Giroux">Henry Giroux</a>, one of the founding theorists of <a href="/wiki/Critical_pedagogy" title="Critical pedagogy">critical pedagogy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> A prominent alumnus in the field of social sciences was <a href="/wiki/Harold_Innis" title="Harold Innis">Harold Innis</a>, who helped shape <a href="/wiki/Communication_theory" title="Communication theory">communication theory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Staples_thesis" title="Staples thesis">staples thesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roy_Kellock" title="Roy Kellock">Roy Kellock</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Justices_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="List of Justices of the Supreme Court of Canada">Justice</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a> was also a graduate from the university.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A significant number of prominent business leaders have studied at McMaster. Examples include <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Elop" title="Stephen Elop">Stephen Elop</a>, current president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> and former president of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s business division;<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_D._House" title="Paul D. House">Paul D. House</a>, current executive chairman of <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons" title="Tim Hortons">Tim Hortons</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lynton_Wilson" title="Lynton Wilson">Lynton Wilson</a>, current chairman of <a href="/wiki/Nortel" title="Nortel">Nortel</a> and chancellor of McMaster;<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Lee-Chin" title="Michael Lee-Chin">Michael Lee-Chin</a>, current chairman, CEO, and <a href="/wiki/Chief_investment_officer" title="Chief investment officer">CIO</a> of <a href="/wiki/AIC_Limited" title="AIC Limited">AIC Limited</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Burgess" title="Rob Burgess">Rob Burgess</a>, former chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Macromedia" title="Macromedia">Macromedia</a> and director of <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Two members of McMaster University had travelled in space: faculty member <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Williams" title="Dafydd Williams">Dafydd Williams</a>, who is a physician-scientist at McMaster Centre for Medical Robotics at <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_Healthcare_Hamilton" title="St. Joseph's Healthcare Hamilton">St. Joseph's Healthcare Hamilton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> and astronaut <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Bondar" title="Roberta Bondar">Roberta Bondar</a>, the first Canadian woman in space.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
